## **FOREWORD** 

The **2023 Full Year Official Poverty Statistics** presents the poverty statistics for 2023 based on the preliminary results of the 2023 Family Income and Expenditure Survey (FIES) conducted by the Philippine Statistics Authority (PSA). National, regional, provincial, and highly urbanized city poverty estimates are generated based on the methodology approved by the PSA Board through Resolution No. 1, Series of 2017 – 171 ( _NSCB Resolution No. 09, Series of 2011 – Approving the Refinements in the Official Poverty Estimation Methodology_ ), which utilizes income data from the FIES to estimate the official poverty statistics. 

The statistical tables on important poverty information for 2018, 2021, and 2023 includes the food and poverty thresholds, subsistence and poverty incidences among families and among population, as well as other useful poverty indicators such as income gap, poverty gap, and severity of poverty. Back estimates for Negros Island Region for 2018 and 2021, and 2023 estimates for Maguindanao del Norte and Maguindanao del Sur are also included in this report. 

The PSA extends its deepest appreciation to the individuals and organizations involved in the two data collection rounds of the 2023 FIES. Immense appreciation is also expressed to the over 160,000 respondents whose information, time, and effort during the data collection were instrumental in the success of the survey. 

The PSA hopes this report serves as a valuable resource for the general public, particularly researchers, program developers, and policymakers. By providing comprehensive data, we aim to support the development and improvement of targeted poverty reduction strategies. 

**CLAIRE DENNIS S. MAPA, PhD** Undersecretary National Statistician and Civil Registrar General 

## **Highlights of the 2023 Full Year Official Poverty Statistics** 

## **A. National** 

## **1. Key Indicators** 

## **Poverty Threshold and Food Threshold** 

In 2023, the poverty threshold for a family with five members at the national level was estimated at PhP 13,873 per month. This amount represents the minimum income required by a family to meet their basic food and non-food needs. The 2023 poverty threshold marks a 15.6 percent increase from the 2021 threshold, which was estimated at PhP 11,998. (Table 1) 

Meanwhile, the food threshold, or the minimum amount required by a family with five members to meet their basic food needs, was estimated at PhP 9,581 per month in 2023. This reflects a 14.7 percent increase compared to the 2021 food threshold. (Table 1) 

The Annual Per Capita Poverty and Food Thresholds by province are presented in the 2023 Full Year Official Poverty Statistics report. 

## **Poverty Incidence and Subsistence Incidence** 

In 2023, the poverty incidence among families was recorded at 10.9 percent at the national level. This translates to 2.99 million poor families whose incomes fell below the poverty threshold. In terms of population, the poverty incidence was estimated at 15.5 percent, equating to 17.54 million Filipinos who were unable to meet their basic food and non-food needs in 2023. 

The subsistence incidence, which is the proportion of families with income less than the food threshold, stood at 2.7 percent in 2023. This translates to 0.74 million families without enough income to meet their basic food needs. Among the population, the subsistence incidence was estimated at 4.3 percent, translating to around 4.84 million Filipinos. (Table 1)

## **2. Other Poverty Measures** 

In addition to these indicators, other poverty measures generated by the Philippine Statistics Authority include the income gap, poverty gap, and squared poverty gap (severity of poverty). 

The income gap, which measures the average amount of income needed by the poor to escape poverty, was estimated at 20.6 percent in 2023. On average, a poor family with five members required an additional monthly income of around PhP 2,859 to rise above the poverty line. This measure is useful for determining the budget needed to lift families out of poverty. (Table 2) 

## **Table 2. Income Gap, Poverty Gap, and Severity of Poverty: 2018, 2021 and 2023**

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the income gap, poverty gap and severity of poverty between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). Source: Philippine Statistics Authority 

## **B. Regional** 

At the sub-national level, the National Capital Region (NCR) continued to have the lowest poverty incidence among families at 1.1 percent in 2023. In contrast, Region IX (Zamboanga Peninsula) had the highest poverty incidence among families at 24.2 percent, followed by the Bangsamoro Autonomous Region in Muslim Mindanao (BARMM) at 23.5 percent and the Negros Island Region (NIR) at 22.6 percent. 

Out of the 18 regions, 11 recorded significant decreases in poverty incidence among families from 2021 to 2023. Caraga had the most notable improvement, with a poverty incidence among families decreasing from 25.9 percent in 2021 to 14.9 percent in 2023. However, increasing trends in poverty incidence were observed in the regions of MIMAROPA (1.2 percentage point increase), NIR (4.4 percentage point increase), and Region IX (Zamboanga Peninsula) (0.8 percentage point increase). Among these, only the NIR showed a statistically significant increase in poverty incidence from 2021 to 2023. (Table 3)

## **C. Provincial** 

At the provincial level, as the PSA does not encourage ranking of provinces in consideration of possible overlapping confidence intervals, provinces were grouped based on their poverty incidence among families.  The provinces were grouped as follows: 

- **Group 1** - poverty incidence among families is greater than or equal to 50% 

- **Group 2** - poverty incidence among families is greater than or equal to 40% but less than 50% 

- **Group 3** - poverty incidence among families is greater than or equal to 30% but less than 40% 

- **Group 4** - poverty incidence among families is greater than or equal to 20% but less than 30% 

- **Group 5** - poverty incidence among families is greater than or equal to 10% but less than 20% 

- **Group 6** -  poverty incidence among families is greater than or equal to 0% but less than 10%

Several provinces maintained their place among the least poor group in both 2021 and 2023, including all districts of NCR, Apayao, Bataan, Batanes, Batangas, Benguet, Bulacan, Cagayan, Capiz, Cavite, Davao del Norte, Davao del Sur, Guimaras, Ifugao, Ilocos Norte, Kalinga, La Union, and Laguna. New additions to this group in 2023 include Abra, Aklan, Biliran, Camiguin, Davao de Oro, Ilocos Sur, Isabela, Marinduque, Nueva Ecija, and Nueva Vizcaya. (Table 4)

Conversely, Basilan, Cotabato City, Maguindanao, Tawi-Tawi, and Zamboanga del Norte were included in the group of provinces with the highest poverty incidence among families in 2023. (Table 5) 

## **D. Highly Urbanized Cities** 

Among highly urbanized cities, including the municipality of Pateros, 31 out of 34 reported single-digit poverty estimates in 2023. Butuan City had the most significant improvement, with poverty incidence among families decreasing from 22.6 percent in 2021 to 12.2 percent in 2023. (Table 6)

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among families between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among families between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among families between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates. 

Source: Philippine Statistics Authority

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of poor families. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

- r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

- 1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among families between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among families between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among families between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

- 5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of poor population. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

- r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among population between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among population between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty incidence among population between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

- 5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** -  Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of food poor families. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

- r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among families between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among families between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among families between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its very small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of food poor families. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

- r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among families between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among families between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among families between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

- 5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among population between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among population between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among population between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

* - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its very small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of food poor population. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

- r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among population between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among population between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the subsistence incidence among population between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its very small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of poor families. 

r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of poor families between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of poor families between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of poor families between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of poor population. 

r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of poor population between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of poor population between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of poor population between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of food poor families. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu.

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor families between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor families between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor families between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

- 5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of food poor families. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

- r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor families between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor families between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor families between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

- 5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of food poor population. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

- r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor population between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor population between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the magnitude of subsistence poor population between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

- 5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021. 

- a/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2018 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- b/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2021 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- c/ Those with CVs higher than 10% in 2023 poverty incidence among families should be used with caution. 

- d/ Coefficient of variation (CV) and standard error (SE) are measures of precision of the estimates.

Notes: 

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of income gap. 

- r1 - Updated 2021 poverty statistics for the national, BARMM and Sulu due to updates in the food prices of Sulu. 

r2 - Revised 2018 and 2021 poverty statistics of Regions VI and VII due to the creation of the Negros Island Region based on Executive Order (EO) No. 183. 

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the income gap between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the income gap between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the income gap between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021.

- - Caution must be observed in utilizing the estimate for this HUC due to its small sample size in 2018, 2021 and 2023. 

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of poverty gap.

1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty gap between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty gap between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the poverty gap between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05).

- ** - Please note that the estimate with dash (-) does not pertain to absolute zero and does not categorically mean the non-existence of severity of poverty.

- 1/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the severity of poverty between 2018 and 2021 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

2/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the severity of poverty between 2021 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

3/ significant change; The increase or decrease in the severity of poverty between 2018 and 2023 is significant at 5% level of significance (α = 0.05). 

- 4/ Excludes 63 barangays transferred to BARMM in 2023. 

- 5/ Excludes 63 barangays from Region XII in 2018 and 2021.

- d/ The groupings of poverty incidences are the following: 

- _**Group 1** - poverty incidence among families is_ _**greater than or equal to 50%** ._ 

- _**Group 2** - poverty incidence among families is_ _**greater than or equal to 40% but less than 50%** ._ _**Group 3** - poverty incidence among families is_ _**greater than or equal to 30% but less than 40%** ._ _**Group 4** - poverty incidence among families is_ _**greater than or equal to 20% but less than 30%** ._ _**Group 5** - poverty incidence among families is_ _**greater than or equal to 10% but less than 20%** ._ _**Group 6** - poverty incidence among families is_ _**greater than or equal to 0% but less than 10%** ._

## **Glossary of Terms** 

- a) **Food threshold** - the minimum income required for a family/individual to meet the basic food needs, which satisfies the nutritional requirements for economically necessary and socially desirable physical activities 

- b) **Income Gap** - the average income shortfall (expressed in proportion to the poverty threshold) of families/individuals with income below the poverty threshold divided by the total number of poor families/individuals 

Note: The difference between the income gap and the poverty gap is the use of number of poor families/ individuals as the denominator for the income gap. For the poverty gap, the total number of families/individuals is used. 

- c) **Poverty gap** - the total income shortfall (expressed in proportion to the poverty threshold) of families/ individuals with income below the poverty threshold divided by the total number of families/ individuals 

- d) **Poverty incidence** - the proportion of families/individuals with per capita income less than the per capita poverty threshold to the total number of families/individuals. 

- e) **Poverty threshold** -  the minimum income required for a family/individual to meet the basic food and non-food requirements 

Note: Basic food requirements are currently based on 100% adequacy for the Recommended Energy and Nutrient Intake (RENI) for protein and energy equivalent to an average of 2000 kilocalories per capita, and 80% adequacy for other nutrients. On the other hand, basic non-food requirements, indirectly estimated by obtaining the ratio of food to total basic expenditures from a reference group of families, cover expenditures on: 1) clothing and footwear; 2) housing; 3) fuel, light, water; 4) maintenance and minor repairs; 5) rental of occupied dwelling units; 6) medical care; 7) education; 8) transportation and communication; 9) non-durable furnishings; 10) household operations; and 11) personal care & effects. 

- f) **Severity of poverty** - the total of the squared income shortfall (expressed in proportion to the poverty threshold) of families/ individuals with income below the poverty threshold divided by the total number of families/ individuals 

Note: This is equal to the Foster-Greer-Thorbecke (FGT) family of measures with alpha = 2. It is a poverty measure, which is sensitive to the income distribution among the poor – the worse this distribution is, the more severe poverty is. 

- g) **Subsistence incidence** - the proportion of families/individuals with per capita income less than the per capita food threshold to the total number of families/individuals 

99 

## _**TECHNICAL NOTES ON THE 2023 FULL YEAR OFFICIAL POVERTY ESTIMATION METHODOLOGY**_ 

## **I. INTRODUCTION** 

The first official methodology for the poverty assessment in the Philippines was adopted in 1987. Three major refinements in the official methodology for measuring poverty have been made in 1992, 2003/2005/2006 and 2011. 

One major feature of the first refinement in 1992 was the exclusion of alcohol, tobacco, recreation, durable furniture, and equipment as well as other miscellaneous expenditures in the list of basic non-food requirements considered in the determination of the poverty line/threshold. Poverty line/threshold refers to the minimum income/expenditure required to meet the basic food and non-food requirements. 

In 2003, another improvement was introduced in recognition of the need for poverty estimates with lower levels of disaggregation, specifically at the provincial level. Using the same regional food bundles in the 1987 and 1992 methodologies developed by the Food and Nutrition Research Institute (FNRI), provincial food thresholds were generated using actual provincial prices collected by then National Statistics Office, which is now part of the Philippine Statistics Authority (PSA). 

The latest refinements in the official poverty estimation methodology were approved in 2011 through PSA Board Resolution No.  1, Series of 2017-171, _Approving the Refinements in the Official Poverty Estimation Methodology_ , to address some issues/ concerns raised in the estimation of food and poverty thresholds, incidence and other measures of poverty, the relevance of official poverty statistics and the comparability of poverty estimates across space and over time. The refinements were based on the recommendations of the Technical Committee on Poverty Statistics (TC PovStat), who were designated to develop/formulate the official poverty estimation methodology. To address the comparability across space and over time, a national reference food bundle was developed as basis for provincial food bundles. The provincial food bundles that were adopted were subjected to the Test of Revealed Preferences, such that the food bundle of a province will have the cheapest cost in comparison with using the bundles of other provinces and also eaten in the province.  In addition, a constant food expenditure to total basic expenditure (FE/TBE) ratio is to be used for ten years. The PSA Board Resolution included a provision that the methodology shall be reviewed every ten (10) years to ensure relevance and accuracy.  This methodology has been used since its approval in 2011. As of 2023, the methodology is currently being reviewed by the TC PovStat. 

100 

## **II. COMPILATION METHODOLOGY** 

## **A. Unit of Measure** 

|**Indicator**|**Unit of measure**|
|---|---|
|Food threshold|Php; using current prices, usually per capita or per<br>person in a year)|
|Subsistence incidence|Percent; in terms of families and population|
|Poverty threshold|Php; using current prices, usually per capita or per<br>person in a year)|
|Poverty incidence|Percent; in terms of families and population|



## **B. Coverage** 

|**Indicator**|**Coverage**|
|---|---|
|Food threshold|National, regional, provincial (with urban-rural areas),<br>and highly urbanized city (HUC) levels|
|Subsistence incidence|National, regional, provincial, and HUC levels|
|Poverty threshold|National, regional, provincial (with urban-rural areas),<br>and HUC levels|
|Poverty incidence|National, regional, provincial, and HUC levels|
|Other measures of poverty<br>(poverty gap, income gap,<br>severity of poverty)|National, regional, provincial, and HUC levels|



## **C. Estimation and Compilation Methodology** 

## _**1. Estimation of Food Threshold**_ 

- a) The use of a national reference food bundle as starting point – to enhance comparability across space. 

- b) The national reference food bundle was converted to province-specific food bundles, which were used to estimate the provincial food thresholds. These provincial food bundles were formulated by nutritionists from the FNRI and were subjected to the Test of Revealed Preferences such that the food bundle of a province will have the cheapest cost in comparison with the bundles of other provinces.  The provincial food bundles have the following characteristics: 

   - Nutritionally adequate, i.e., it satisfies the 100% Recommended Energy and Nutrient Intake (RENI) for energy and protein and 80% RENI for other vitamins and minerals; 

   - Food items in the food bundle are locally available and eaten in the area (in the province); 

   - Least cost in the province; and 

   - Visualizable (i.e., can be cooked together and fit for human consumption). 

## c) Sources of data: 

- Provincial food bundles developed by FNRI 

- Retail price surveys for the actual prices of agricultural and non-agricultural commodities, by province from PSA 

- Proportion of food bought and own-produced components from the Food Consumption Survey, FNRI 

101 

## d) General Procedures: 

- Each of the ingredients in the food bundle is priced using the available price data (average price from January to December) 

- The urban and rural food thresholds for each of the provinces, which have bought and own-produced components, are computed. 

- The provincial urban/rural annual per capita food threshold/line is computed as: 

   - FT = (cost per capita of the one-day food bundle) x (30.4 days/month) x 12 months 

## _**2. Estimation of Subsistence Incidence**_ 

- Given the provincial urban-rural food threshold, the subsistence incidence is computed as: 

**==> picture [76 x 27] intentionally omitted <==**

where: 

- F = weighted total number of families (individuals) with annual per capita income less than the provincial urban-rural annual per capita food threshold/line 

- n = weighted total number of families (individuals) in the province 

## _**3. Estimation of Poverty Thresholds**_ 

- a) As common practice in most countries, the non-food component is measured indirectly due to the difficulty of determining the required bundle for the nonfood items. 

- b) To ensure comparability across space and over time, the ratio of food expenditures (FE) to total basic expenditures (TBE) of a reference family (families whose per capita income is around the food threshold) is held constant for a certain period. The average of the nationally determined FE/TBE ratio from the FIES in 2000, 2003, 2006 and 2009, which is equivalent to 0.6983, has been used since 2009 and still being used until 2023. 

- c) Sources of data: 

   - The 2023 FIES was collected through two visits.  Visit 1 was conducted in July 2023 for the collection of data for the reference period of January to June 2023 while Visit 2 was conducted in January 2024 for the second semester data. The total number of completed samples was 163,256 families spread across 118 sampling domains around the country. This large sample size can provide reliable estimates at the national, regional, provincial, and HUC levels. 

102 

## d) General Procedures: 

- _The urban/rural provincial poverty threshold is computed by dividing the food threshold with the FE/TBE ratio._ 

𝑃𝑜𝑣𝑒𝑟𝑡𝑦 𝑇ℎ𝑟𝑒𝑠ℎ𝑜𝑙𝑑=[𝐹𝑜𝑜𝑑 𝑇ℎ𝑟𝑒𝑠ℎ𝑜𝑙𝑑] 𝐹𝐸 𝑇𝐵𝐸 where: 𝐹𝐸 = 0.6983 𝑇𝐵𝐸 

- FE = actual food expenditure of families within the +/- ten percentile band of the subsistence incidence among families 

TBE = total basic expenditure of families within the +/- ten percentile band of the subsistence incidence among families. TBE is an aggregate of expenditures on 

- food 

- clothing and footwear 

- fuel; light and water 

- housing maintenance and other minor repairs 

- rental of occupied dwelling units 

- medical care 

- education 

- transportation and communication 

- non-durable furnishing 

- household operations; and 

- personal care and effects 

## _**4. Estimation of Poverty Incidence**_ 

- Given the provincial urban-rural poverty threshold, the poverty incidence is computed as: 

**==> picture [64 x 26] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
𝑃=  [𝑄] ∗100<br>𝑛<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


where: 

- Q = weighted total number of families (individuals) with annual per capita income less than the annual per capita poverty threshold/line 

- n = weighted total number of families (individuals) 

103 

_**5. Estimation of other measures of poverty such as Income Gap (I), Poverty Gap (PG) and Severity of Poverty (SP)**_ 

## **Income Gap** 

- the weighted average income shortfall (expressed in proportion to the poverty threshold) of families/individuals with income below the provincial urban-rural poverty threshold. 

**==> picture [142 x 40] intentionally omitted <==**

where: Z = provincial urban-rural per capita poverty threshold/line 𝑋𝑖 = per capita income of the i[th] family q = number of families below the poverty threshold 

## **Poverty Gap** 

- the weighted total income shortfall (expressed in proportion to the poverty threshold) of families/individuals with income below the poverty threshold divided by the weighted total number of families/ individuals 

𝑞 𝑃𝑜𝑣𝑒𝑟𝑡𝑦 𝑔𝑎𝑝=[1] 𝑛 ∑[𝑍−𝑋] 𝑍[𝑖] 𝑖=1 

- where: Z = provincial urban-rural per capita poverty threshold/line 𝑋𝑖 = per capita income of the i[th] family q = number of families below the poverty threshold n = total number of families 

Note: The difference between the income gap and the poverty gap is on the denominator. For the income gap, the denominator is the number of poor families/individuals. For the poverty gap, the total number of families/individuals is used. 

## **Severity Gap** 

- the weighted total of the squared income shortfall (expressed in proportion to the poverty threshold) of families/individuals with income below the poverty threshold, divided by the weighted total number of families/individuals 

**==> picture [161 x 40] intentionally omitted <==**

where: 

- Z = per capita poverty threshold/line 𝑋𝑖 = per capita income of the i[th] family q = weighted total number of families below the poverty threshold n = weighted total number of families 

104 

## _**Measures of Precision**_ 

- a. The official poverty statistics shall be released with measures of precision such as standard errors, confidence intervals and coefficients of variation. 

- b. Ranking of provinces shall not be released due to overlapping confidence intervals. Grouping of provinces based on the poverty incidence among families shall be released instead.
